Source Code

000001,000001:                                                                                                 #  Copyright:     Public domain.
000002,000002:                                                                                                 #  Filename:      MAIN.agc
000003,000003:                                                                                                 #  Purpose:       Part of the source code for Colossus 2A, AKA Comanche 055.
000004,000004:                                                                                                 #                 It is part of the source code for the Command Module's (CM)
000005,000005:                                                                                                 #                 Apollo Guidance Computer (AGC) Apollo 11.
000006,000006:                                                                                                 #  Assembler:     yaYUL
000007,000007:                                                                                                 #  Contact:       Ron Burkey <info@sandroid.org>.
000008,000008:                                                                                                 #  Website:       www.ibiblio.org/apollo
000009,000009:                                                                                                 #  Mod history:   2009-05-05 RSB  Adapted from Colossus249/MAIN.agc.
000010,000010: 
000011,000011:                                                                                                 #  This source code has been transcribed or otherwise adapted from digitized
000012,000012:                                                                                                 #  images of a hardcopy from the MIT Museum.  The digitization was performed
000013,000013:                                                                                                 #  by Paul Fjeld, and arranged for by Deborah Douglas of the Museum.  Many
000014,000014:                                                                                                 #  thanks to both.  The images (with suitable reduction in storage size and
000015,000015:                                                                                                 #  consequent reduction in image quality as well) are available online at
000016,000016:                                                                                                 #  www.ibiblio.org/apollo.  If for some reason you find that the images are
000017,000017:                                                                                                 #  illegible, contact me at info@sandroid.org about getting access to the 
000018,000018:                                                                                                 #  (much) higher-quality images which Paul actually created.
000019,000019: 
000020,000020:                                                                                                 #  Notations on the hardcopy document read, in part:
000021,000021: 
000022,000022:                                                                                                 #         Assemble revision 055 of AGC program Comanche by NASA
000023,000023:                                                                                                 #         2021113-051.  10:28 APR. 1, 1969  
000024,000024: 
000025,000025:                                                                                                 #         This AGC program shall also be referred to as
000026,000026:                                                                                                 #                         Colossus 2A
000027,000027: 
000028,000028:                                                                                                 #  This file is a little different from the other Comanche055 files I'm providing, 
000029,000029:                                                                                                 #  in that it doesn't represent anything that appears directly in the original source.  
000030,000030:                                                                                                 #  What I (RSB) have done for organizational purposes is to split the huge monolithic
000031,000031:                                                                                                 #  source code into smaller, more manageable chunks--i.e., into individual source 
000032,000032:                                                                                                 #  files.  Those files are rejoined within this file as "includes".  It just makes
000033,000033:                                                                                                 #  it a little easier to work with.  The code chunks correspond to natural divisions
000034,000034:                                                                                                 #  into sub-programs.  In fact, these divisions are more-or-less specified by
000035,000035:                                                                                                 #  the source code itself.  Refer to the "SUBROUTINE CALLS" at the
000036,000036:                                                                                                 #  very beginning of the file ASSEMBLY_AND_OPERATION_INFORMATION.agc.
000037,000037: 
000038,000038:                                                                                                 #  It may be reasonably asked why tens of thousands of lines of source are joined by
000039,000039:                                                                                                 #  means of inclusion, rather than simply assembling the source files individually and
000040,000040:                                                                                                 #  then linking them to form the executable.  The answer is that the original 
000041,000041:                                                                                                 #  development team had no linker.  The builds were monolithic just like this.
000042,000042:                                                                                                 #  There was a big emphasis on reusability of the code in the original project, 
000043,000043:                                                                                                 #  apparently, but this reusability took the form of inserting your deck of 
000044,000044:                                                                                                 #  punch-cards at the appropriate position in somebody else's deck of punch-cards.
000045,000045:                                                                                                 #  (Actually, I think the card-decks were turned into tape libraries, and the modules
000046,000046:                                                                                                 #  were mixed-and-matched from the tape libraries, but the principle is the same.)
000047,000047:                                                                                                 #  So, indeed, the method of file-inclusion is a very fair representation of the 
000048,000048:                                                                                                 #  methods used in the original development ... with the improvement, of course,
000049,000049:                                                                                                 #  that you no longer have to worry about dropping the card deck.  On the other hand, 
000050,000050:                                                                                                 #  I wasn't there at the time, so I may have no idea what I'm talking about.
000051,000051: 
000052,000052:                                                                                                 #  Finally, note that the original Apollo AGC assembler (called "YUL") is no longer 
000053,000053:                                                                                                 #  available (as far as I can tell).  Actually, it had already been replaced by another
000054,000054:                                                                                                 #  assembler (called "GAP") by the time of Apollo 11, but GAP isn't available either.
000055,000055:                                                                                                 #  The replacement assembler yaYUL accepts a slightly different format for the source 
000056,000056:                                                                                                 #  code from what YUL or GAP accepted, so the source code has been targeted for 
000057,000057:                                                                                                 #  assembly with yaYUL.
000058,000058: 
000059,000059:                                                                                                 #  What follows is simply a bunch of file-includes for the individual code chunks.
000060,000060:                                                                                                 #  I've marked the page numbers to make proof-reading easier.  The page images also
000061,000061:                                                                                                 #  contain a lot of interesting tables (cross-referenced to page numbers) created by GAP, 
000062,000062:                                                                                                 #  but not duplicated by yaYUL, so it's still valuable even if the source-files
000063,000063:                                                                                                 #  listed below are in hand.
000064,000064:
